<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_54f5b6d5-a540-4c53-8d44-4737a3faf4f8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

    <a title="L A i N E Y" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y"><img alt="L A i N E Y" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546138360p2/10752235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1908564183?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857560025" href="/book/show/10637825-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1908564183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12375555121150649536">This book was a piece of heaven for my little bruising shipping heart... <br/><br/>One of the most achingly beautiful moments for YA couples ever. But I kept reading and it happened again - a scene more memorable than the last. By the time I'm close to finish this was my thought "o<i>kay</i> this is getting ridiculous". <b>Tenderest of moments upon even more lovely scenes, both together and apart,</b> I just...... it was hard to comprehend how much I felt for these two. <br/><br/><br/><br/>I made this sounds like a fluffy, romance-heavy b</span>
  <span id="freeText12375555121150649536" style="display:none">This book was a piece of heaven for my little bruising shipping heart... <br /><br />One of the most achingly beautiful moments for YA couples ever. But I kept reading and it happened again - a scene more memorable than the last. By the time I'm close to finish this was my thought "o<i>kay</i> this is getting ridiculous". <b>Tenderest of moments upon even more lovely scenes, both together and apart,</b> I just...... it was hard to comprehend how much I felt for these two. <br /><br /><br /><br />I made this sounds like a fluffy, romance-heavy book and it was while also <i>wasn't.</i> The romance wasn't strictly romantic type - it's a lot to do with family and friends and how much you'd do for them. <br /><br /><br />It was a uniquely brave book. <br /><br />And I won't be able to get over this book hangover any time soon.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12375555121150649536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115777962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115777962" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115777962?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385751605" href="/book/show/9972776-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2011">starred-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=4">4</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115777962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699998912225827895">3.5 stars.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me' title='You Against Me by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>You Against Me</a> was one of my most anticipated books of 2011. So much so that I was 100% sure I would give it 5 stars. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/628636.Jenny_Downham' title='Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Downham</a>'s debut <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die' title='Before I Die by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Die</a> left me a sobbing mess (I am in a minority here thought, most of my co-readers did not join the cryfest). I expected the same from her second novel. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me' title='You Against Me by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>You Against Me</a> was good, just not as good as it could have been.<br/><br/>Let me just say, the plot itself is fantastic. The two main characters in this love story - Mikey and Ellie - have a very co</span>
  <span id="freeText3699998912225827895" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me" title="You Against Me by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">You Against Me</a> was one of my most anticipated books of 2011. So much so that I was 100% sure I would give it 5 stars. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/628636.Jenny_Downham" title="Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Downham</a>'s debut <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die" title="Before I Die by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Die</a> left me a sobbing mess (I am in a minority here thought, most of my co-readers did not join the cryfest). I expected the same from her second novel. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me" title="You Against Me by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">You Against Me</a> was good, just not as good as it could have been.<br /><br />Let me just say, the plot itself is fantastic. The two main characters in this love story - Mikey and Ellie - have a very complicated relationship. Mikey's 15-year old sister is a rape victim. Her alleged abuser is Ellie's older brother. Mikey is a protective brother and is determined to punish the rapist. Ellie loves her own brother and wants to believe in his innocent. The two teens first come together to get information out of each other, to help their families, but soon their loyalties and beliefs start shifting.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me" title="You Against Me by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">You Against Me</a> portrays the issue of rape with care and sensitivity, in all its complexity. Downham shows that the families of both the victim and her assailant are affected by the crime as much as the people directly involved in it. She writes about the denial and blind belief of the rapist's family and the exhaustion and even some blaming in the family of the victim. She shows how easy it is to discredit a rape victim by labeling her a slut - a short skirt, some drinking and any kind of dating history is all it takes. How hard it is to prove that she didn't "ask for it" in a drunken stupor. And that a victim's ordeal doesn't end with a filing of a police report.<br /><br />As much as I appreciated all this in the novel, I wish it were more intense, tighter. It needed not to be so quiet, so subdued, it needed more outrage, more drama. It needed to push more boundaries. It needed to shear off 50 or so pages in the middle. It needed to make me care about the romance and characters more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3699998912225827895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_218104311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218104311" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218104311?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218104311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14028689462860815841"><b>
  <i>“It was strange how words meant something when they came out of your mouth. Inside your head they were safe and silent, but once they were outside, people grabbed hold of them.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>Wow, what beautiful ending. And book, actually. Extremely unique, fascinating and honest.<br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>Ellie. Mike. Trust. Doubt. Truth. Lies. Perception. Bracing rivers. Baked potatoes. Old cottages. Bunking classes. Cookery. The future. Team Karyn. <br/><b><br/>Low Points.</b><br/>Even though I liked the romance</span>
  <span id="freeText14028689462860815841" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“It was strange how words meant something when they came out of your mouth. Inside your head they were safe and silent, but once they were outside, people grabbed hold of them.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />Wow, what beautiful ending. And book, actually. Extremely unique, fascinating and honest.<br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />Ellie. Mike. Trust. Doubt. Truth. Lies. Perception. Bracing rivers. Baked potatoes. Old cottages. Bunking classes. Cookery. The future. Team Karyn. <br /><b><br />Low Points.</b><br />Even though I liked the romance between Mikey and Ellie, I’m not sure whether it would have progressed so quickly in reality. I think, with a subject matter like this one, there would have been a lot more anger in there and it would have taken longer for them to turn to each other and realised how they felt. <br />I kept getting muddled with how much time had gone past in this book, it could have been a little clearer. <br />But that’s only a little quibble- the rest was absolutely brilliant.<br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />Oh Ellie. You had me conflicted throughout most of this book. One chapter I thought you were ok, the next I loved you, the next chapter I was screaming ‘Ew, if you’re going to come back fighting don’t liken yourself to Jean fricken Grey. Do you not remember how that ended?!', and then I hated her. Really hated her. And then I loved her again. <br />And I ended on loving her.<br />Ms Downham did a beautiful job with Ellie, a girl in an unimaginable and horrific situation.<br />But Ellie, my love, stop jumping in rivers. Yes, it sounds fun and edgy and cool but we live in <i>Britain</i> and you’ll catch your death. <br /><br /><b>Hero.</b> <br />Mikey, mind if I call you Mike? I don’t like the name Mikey, it makes you sound about five.<br />I was a bit worried about you first, partly because you were playing a dangerous game with Ellie and also you were carrying a spanner. Which is never good.<br />But then I warmed up to you as the book went on… and I mean <i>really</i> warmed up to you. <br />You’re a bit of a <i>one</i>, you make no apologies, you’re loyal to your family, you’re sweet with Ellie and your friends, you have dreams and you know how to cook.<br />I didn’t hinder that I was totally picturing you as a Tony Stonem. Boom.<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune. </b><br />This was a difficult song to choose because, as I’ve mentioned before, there were so many issues and emotions covered. But I’ve decided to focus on the, as Mikey said, the best thing that came out of this whole thing. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fcVVDYzwQio" rel="nofollow noopener">You Make it Easy by Air.</a><br /><blockquote><br />“He felt perfectly happy as he walked side by side with Ellie, their fingers occasionally brushing, electricity building between them. It was the first time in days, maybe the first time in all his life, that he didn’t want to change anything.”<br /></blockquote><br /><br /><br />This book wasn’t a love story… but there was definitely love in it. <br /><br /><b>Sadness Scale.</b><br />9/10.<br />It would be really easy to dismiss this book as a modern Romeo &amp; Juliet story (If it had believe me, this book would have been flung out of the window so hard) and about teenagers coming together in exceptional circumstances. But as much as I liked their relationship and it was sweet and tactfully done, I felt this story was about so much more than that. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If a girl is drunk and is raped, it’s her fault because she was the one who put herself into that situation, right? Or if she chooses to wear short skirts she’s obviously “asking for it”, right? If a girl has had previous sexual partners she obvious wants to have sex with everyone, right? And if she goes around to a boy’s house it’s an invitation for him to do as he pleases… right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />It is horrific to think that these thoughts occur at all, never mind how often they actually do. <br />It’s a complex story about loss, fear, justice, allegiance, doubt and trust but Downham explores them all to great depth with unflinching honesty and respect without ever resorting to manipulating her readers. <br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />Anyone who wants a beautifully written book about a difficult subject matter. People who don’t mind books without definite answers. People who would be quite happy just to paddle in rivers because the water is freezing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14028689462860815841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_238667380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238667380" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238667380?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=distant-lands">distant-lands</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238667380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16815108525157731809">i feel such pressure to write a really great review for this book, because it is so impressive on so many levels, but the post-turkey-day fatigue is strong in me. i will do what i can.<br/><br/>you probably already know what this book is about, because it is really quite popular. so just quickly. to get us all on the same page, i will just reiterate that it is a story bout a rape, from the perspective of the brother of the victim and the sister of the accused, who form a relationship in the busted pieces </span>
  <span id="freeText16815108525157731809" style="display:none">i feel such pressure to write a really great review for this book, because it is so impressive on so many levels, but the post-turkey-day fatigue is strong in me. i will do what i can.<br><br>you probably already know what this book is about, because it is really quite popular. so just quickly. to get us all on the same page, i will just reiterate that it is a story bout a rape, from the perspective of the brother of the victim and the sister of the accused, who form a relationship in the busted pieces of all of it.<br><br>which is already, like - woah.<br><br>because when you are dealing with this situation, in literature, the impulse is of course to focus on the victim. it is more powerful that way, right? to showcase the pain and the humiliation and the fear and the aftermath and how one goes about picking up the pieces of their life in a situation like that.<br><br>not so.<br><br>because here, on the outskirts, the ripples are just as strong, and this book does such an amazing job of depicting how rape affects people on the periphery of the situation - people who were not even present at the time - in such profound ways. <br><br>mikey's impulse is to protect his sister, and to physically destroy the boy who did this to her. ellie's impulse is to stick loyally to her family, and believe her brother when he says he is innocent.<br><br>exactly zero of the characters in this book are sympathetic or likable, but the writing overpowers their broad impotent rage or their wishy-washiness or their latent sexism or their naiveté. you will get sucked into the story, despite wanting to give everyone a good smack.<br><br>it is a tricky book, filled with nuance. mikey's easy seduction of girls he feels nothing for starts to pall for him in the aftermath of his sister's rape, leaving him wide open to fall for ellie, despite his intentions of manipulating her into giving him access to her brother tommy, for his deserved ass-beating. he does sort of start to understand that his own behavior towards women has been distasteful, but he continues to focus on violence as a way of solving his problems, instead of really being there for his sister. he does the things that need to be done to hold his family together while his mother drowns in alcohol and absentee parenthood and his sister refuses to leave the house, but it is surface-only; mechanical. he forgets about the root of the problem, wrapped up in some antiquated code of vengeance, and neglects to support his sister emotionally, so focused on hatred as he is.<br><br>ellie is another crappy thing altogether. she is the wide-eyed, overpetted lamb of her surface-perfect wealthy family, idolizing her golden-boy older brother and knowing he could do no wrong. she is so credulous, it hurts. and she is supposed to be this great scholar, but her big idea is to GOOGLE "rape"?? come on, sister, show me those supposed smarts already.<br><br>tommy and ellie's father is one of the worst human beings i have ever read about, as a character. not because he is the manifestation of pure evil, it is more insidious than that. but he reminds me of my ex's father, and it is so appalling to read him. yes, he is protecting his young and that is very admirable, but phoar... the lengths to which he goes and his casual dismissal of this poor girl is really very horrifying. made me want to pull out my hair a little. <br><br>it is also a fantastic book in its treatment of the rape. because it is all he-said, she-said, and it gets difficult. because, again, these are orbital characters, not the main participants. and it isn't a thrown-up-against-the-wall attack, it is much much murkier. and so sad and desperate and emotional. <br><br>this is a very necessary book, unfortunately. and it does its job so well. it has its weak bits, obviously, but the message is such an important one, outside of any bittersweet young love story between two fragile and confused romeo-and-juliet teens. <br><br>this shit is not okay. and i am awfully glad this book is out there for all the young girls who maybe need a book like this. <br><br>best i can do.<br><br>oh, a p.s. for greg. you would like this book because it is all about your beloved british underclass. they eat so many crisps!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16815108525157731809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_145865349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145865349" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145865349?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145865349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10153071270536400125"><br/>Well... finally, a much-anticipated book that actually delivered. After being so hyped up about 'Matched' and then being let down with it's mediocrity, I tried not to get too excited about this book and prepared myself for another monumental disappointment.<br/><br/>But no.<br/><br/>I'm always rather dubious when it comes to romance novels; if you find a good one then you can be reeled in and swallowed up, it can stay with you for a very long time... but so often this is not the case. The amount of times I've dared</span>
  <span id="freeText10153071270536400125" style="display:none"><br>Well... finally, a much-anticipated book that actually delivered. After being so hyped up about 'Matched' and then being let down with it's mediocrity, I tried not to get too excited about this book and prepared myself for another monumental disappointment.<br><br>But no.<br><br>I'm always rather dubious when it comes to romance novels; if you find a good one then you can be reeled in and swallowed up, it can stay with you for a very long time... but so often this is not the case. The amount of times I've dared to enter into a romance story with high hopes and found nothing but cheesy, star-struck "I can't live without you"s are countless. They are often plagued with cliched characters and storylines and I found myself awaiting something similar from 'You Against Me'.<br><br>And I loved it. No, seriously, I really did. The chemistry sparked off the pages without being over-emotionally cheesy. There was no getting lost in their eyes, no "oh gosh, did our hands just accidently touch?"<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345172ra/699913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked and genuinely cared about both characters. Plus, it was so much more than a love story, the dark backdrop of sexual abuse is told through different eyes, tackling the 'slut' issue that is a very real hindrance to prosecutions in rape cases. The fact that anyone can even ask the question: "If a girl is wearing revealing clothing, is she asking for it?" just shows how important this novel is.<br><br>Was it perfect? No. I had an issue with the ending, or lack of if you want to be precise. Perhaps the author was leaving it open for a possible sequel but nothing has been mentioned so far. There are very few cases where ambiguous endings work (The Handmaid's Tale is one) and this book required something more at the end. But I liked it so much that I would happily say yes to that sequel.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10153071270536400125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229193400" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229193400" />
    <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva"><img alt="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392555495p2/1491042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229193400?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva">Aly (Fantasy4eva)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=uk-bookish-love">uk-bookish-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=conflicted-thoughts">conflicted-thoughts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229193400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13310577073339992956">Most seem to love this book. Isn't it annoying when you're the odd one out? :/<br/><br/>Let's get on to my thoughts, shall we! ;)<br/><br/>When Ellie's brother, Tom, is accused of assaulting a girl, his family is pretty supportive and stand by him. The thing is, they're so busy supporting him that they don't even freaking ask him if he actually did it, I mean, talk about baffling! Meanwhile, Mikey' sister, Karyn, has locked herself in her room ever since they found out what happened to her. Both family's lives are </span>
  <span id="freeText13310577073339992956" style="display:none">Most seem to love this book. Isn't it annoying when you're the odd one out? :/<br /><br />Let's get on to my thoughts, shall we! ;)<br /><br />When Ellie's brother, Tom, is accused of assaulting a girl, his family is pretty supportive and stand by him. The thing is, they're so busy supporting him that they don't even freaking ask him if he actually did it, I mean, talk about baffling! Meanwhile, Mikey' sister, Karyn, has locked herself in her room ever since they found out what happened to her. Both family's lives are turned completely upside down.<br /><br />So when Ellie and Mikey happen to meet by chance, although originally, both have ulterior motives, both eventually find themselves falling for each other.<br /><br />Ellie' family is well off in contrast to Mikey' who lives on the rough end of town. Whilst Ellie comes from a tight knit family, Mikey and his sister only have their mum. But even then, it's Mikey who's always been in charge. With his mum venturing out in the late hours of the night and staggering back drunk, the pressure quickly falls on his shoulders. And although I commend him for being responsible and taking care of his sister and mother, there's no doubt that he's just a complete jerk. First off, he simply see's women as meat and has no respect towards any female whatsoever. It Makes him hard to like or care for really. Not to mention he does some really stupid things, and although he improves a lot towards the end, it was a little too late by then.<br /><br />Ellie, on the other hand, is being treated as a suspect. Apparently she was there when it happened, but she claims to have been asleep. Throughout the book you will find yourself grow weary towards her. You really don't know how much you can trust this girl. One piece of advice. Don't fall for her naive little charade. She's more sharp than she lets on. I didn't like her either. Conniving people piss me off.<br /><br />The problem for me was that I couldn't bring myself to care or like even one character. And how could I? Every one of them were either conniving or unlikeable. To top it all off, the slang/accent the characters have going on really grated on me. I've heard it in the past, sure, but when you have to hear it for 300+ pages, it gets a bit too much.<br /><br />Also, I didn't believe that Ellie and Mikey were in love at all. Sure they like each other, but love? Now that's pulling it a stretch.<br /><br />I did like that the book constantly kept you on your toes. You're always questioning whose lying and telling the truth, and I'm glad that you don't find out until the very end. It helped really build up some great tension. <br /><br />It ends as well as it could have. With lingering hope and an air of possibilities.<br /><br />It was an ok read, but I'm not sure I can say that I liked it. ( I had high hopes from loving BEFORE I DIE). I'm sure many will enjoy it more than I did, but I don't think this one is for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13310577073339992956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_247140549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247140549" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247140549?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849920483" href="/book/show/9743803-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Reynje by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247140549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6201014019349086986"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>When I was at the beach as a kid, I used to regularly do this thing where I would swim out as far as I could, just to see how much distance I could cover. I’d swim until my arms got tired, then stop to catch my breath before turning around. I never stopped doing it, but I’d be lying if I said that every single time, I didn’t experience a second of sheer panic when realized I was just suspended there, well and truly <i>out of my depth</i>.<br/><br/>I feel a little like that trying to write this review. (</span>
  <span id="freeText6201014019349086986" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />When I was at the beach as a kid, I used to regularly do this thing where I would swim out as far as I could, just to see how much distance I could cover. I’d swim until my arms got tired, then stop to catch my breath before turning around. I never stopped doing it, but I’d be lying if I said that every single time, I didn’t experience a second of sheer panic when realized I was just suspended there, well and truly <i>out of my depth</i>.<br /><br />I feel a little like that trying to write this review. (Also, ocean swimming is mentioned in this book so I’m not being entirely off topic). I’m sitting here nervously hunched over my keyboard, because I can feel what I want to say, I’m just not entirely sure I’ll be able to articulate it. And You Against Me is a book that takes the reader into deep water, so to speak. I just want to be sure of my footing. <br /><br />I’ve read other books that deal with sexual assault, where the story centres around the emotional and mental journey of a character who has been assaulted. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Most recently, Raw Blue. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />You Against Me is somewhat different in that it focuses on the family members of both the accuser and the accused, how it alters their lives and what happens when revenge and doubt collide. <br /><br />I’ll start by saying that this is a very readable book, and I enjoyed Downham’s particular writing style. It’s pared back, almost stark, and suited to the somber, often bleak atmosphere of the setting and the story. Then there are occasional passages that are unexpectedly expressive and vivid, spots of beauty amid the almost oppressively grim tone. Downham certainly captures the respective worlds her characters live in with unflinching bluntness. It’s particularly effective in juxtaposing the two different socio-economic backgrounds of Mikey and Ellie. In this and other ways it’s a book of contrasts, pushing different sides into conflict and comparison. <br /><br />Downham’s characterisation is also excellent. Mikey, Ellie and the supporting characters felt like real, flawed, somewhat broken people attempting to go about their lives however they knew. None of the characters are particularly “likeable”, but I’d argue that’s not really the point in a book like this. Downham seems to be simply demonstrating what people are capable of, good and bad. I do think that she shows courage in writing her characters this way, allowing her “protagonists”, Mikey and Ellie, to do unsympathetic things. <br /><br />Then there are parts of this book that are outright uncomfortable, sections that I found extremely difficult to read. It’s a horrible truth that victim-blaming is still alive and well in society, and Downham doesn’t back down from showing this. Whether it’s the bald remarks about “slutty” clothing, drinking and girls “asking for it”, or the more subtle but intensely stomach-churning comments Mikey’s mother makes in which she implies that her daughter has brought trouble upon herself and the family by speaking up – none of it is easy to read. <br /><br />I’m very much aware that these kind of things are still said, and that Downham is accurately presenting what sadly happens every day, but to be honest, I struggled with it. There is a fine line between being brutally realistic and propagating a harmful pattern of belief. While victim-blaming and consent is addressed, certain scenes still made me upset. Maybe this was the point - to drag this issue out in the light, to show that these judgments are not okay. Does it succeed? Yes? I think so? I don’t know.<br /><br />Aside from this, You Against Me does a brilliant job of keeping the reader uncertain and unsettled. By forcing her characters in nightmarish circumstances and testing their allegiances to the full extent, I was never quite sure up until the last few pages where it was going to go. <br /><br /> The title is extremely appropriate for this story. Initially, it appears to reference the cross-purposes of Ellie and Mikey. However, as the story evolves, it becomes clear that this expression could be applied to all of the characters at various points, as they are all drawn into the depths of this complex and harrowing situation, particularly as regards family, the urge to protect, and the extent of denial. <br /><br />You Against Me is a challenging and tough book. I have to admire the way Downham tackles the subject matter honestly and openly, and I hope it provokes more conversation and thought about these issues. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6201014019349086986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168757328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168757328" />
    <a title="ivana18" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4939889-ivana18"><img alt="ivana18" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323003480p2/4939889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168757328?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ivana18" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ivana18" href="/user/show/4939889-ivana18">ivana18</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385751605" href="/book/show/9972776-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939889-ivana18?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939889-ivana18?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939889-ivana18?shelf=romance-ya">romance-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168757328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234538633154045478">Thank you very much Law school because if it wasn't for you I wouldn't have had trouble sleeping and I wouldn't have read this book as fast as I did, it definitely deserves to be read in one breath.<br/>This book was an all-nighter, and after I finished it (2:30 AM) I couldn't sleep for at least another hour thinking about it. <br/><br/>One of my first thoughts last night when I finished this book was: <b>Romeo and Juliet meets Crime and Punishment.</b><br/>This is a YA drama, and it's the best YA books I've read so far. </span>
  <span id="freeText6234538633154045478" style="display:none">Thank you very much Law school because if it wasn't for you I wouldn't have had trouble sleeping and I wouldn't have read this book as fast as I did, it definitely deserves to be read in one breath.<br />This book was an all-nighter, and after I finished it (2:30 AM) I couldn't sleep for at least another hour thinking about it. <br /><br />One of my first thoughts last night when I finished this book was: <b>Romeo and Juliet meets Crime and Punishment.</b><br />This is a YA drama, and it's the best YA books I've read so far. It's real and angsty and funny and sweet and heartbreaking and heart-heeling, and it made me cry like a baby.<br /><br />15 year old Karyn McKenzie likes 18 year old Tom Parker. One night they run into each other in a pub and Tom brings Karyn home with him. They drink alcohol and smoke pot. In the morning Karyn goes home, and 24 hours later she goes to the police and accuses Tom of rape.<br /><br />But this story is not really about Karyn and Tom. This story is about Karyn's older brother, 18 year old Mikey McKenzie, and Tom's younger sister, 16 year old Ellie Parker, and the Hell they go trough while trying to deal with Karyn's accusation and Tom's claim that the rape didn't happen. One of them is lying, and in this review I'll try not to hint which one, <b>and I urge other reviewers to do the same, or put spoiler warnings,</b> because for 2/3 of the book we really do not know who's lying and who's telling the truth.<br /><br />Mikey is trying very hard to keep his family together, his mom is an alcoholic and there's no dad to rely on. He looks out for his 2 younger sisters and his messed up mother. He brings food to the house, tries to take his baby sister Holly to school on time, and is trying to help Karyn deal with everything that's happened. He is extremely troubled by the fact that Karyn won't even go out of the flat, and that's she missing so much school that she probably won't graduate. He believes that Karyn's accusation is true. He's angry at Tom and wants justice and revenge. <br /><br />Ellie was at the house that night when Tom brought Karyn and his friends back to party. When the police came for Tom it was like someone tore a piece of her heart. She loves her brother very much and believes him when he says that the rape didn't happen. She'll do anything to save him from being locked up.<br /><br />When Mikey and Ellie meet, their worlds collide. They both love their siblings and are trying to protect them.. Ellie believes her brother's being truthful and Mikey believes Karyn....and somehow, in the midst of it all, they fall in love.<br /><br />I've read some of the other readers reviews and was puzzled by them. It still amazes me that so many people think that the world is black and white, and that it is really easy to tell the difference from right and wrong. <br />Well sometimes there's no right and wrong, there's just wrong and wrong, and it is up to you to choose the lesser evil. Something that Ellie said explains it perfectly: <i>She took her hands away from her face. ‘It isn’t going to be over, don’t you get it? Someone’s family’s going to be ruined – yours or mine, that’s the choice. We can’t run away. This is real life, Mikey!</i> <br />From what I've read it seems that people don't understand Mikey's and Ellie's actions, don't understand why they did what they did in order to save/help their siblings....but I do understand because blood is thicker than water, and love for your family makes you do desperate things, even when you know that what you're doing is wrong. <br /><br />What would you do? How far would you go to save your family?<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Would you lie to save your brother, or your father, or your son from jail? <br />Would you commit perjury in order to keep your family together? <br />Aren't those the type of questions that you can't really give an answer to.... because the father accused of that crime is the same father who loves you and who took care of you.... and that brother is the same big brother who saved your life when a mad dog attacked you and scarred your young face.... and that son is the same son you carried in your womb for 9 months and gave birth to, and every time you look at him you see a sweet baby boy with beautiful golden curls trying to take hist first steps.<br />Would you lie even though you're doubts are driving you crazy and your conscience is screaming at you to tell the truth? What if he didn't do it and your truthful statement could land him in jail? And worst of all, what if he really did do those terrible things?<br /><br />And what if it was your mom, or sister, daughter that was raped and the person that did it is getting away with it. What if you're not really sure about what happened because she won't talk about it. What would you do then?<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />This book brings out a lot of questions. There are no easy answers to these questions. I for one don't know what I would have done if I was in Mikey's or Ellie's place and I pray that I never have to find out the answers for myself.<br />Rape is a very difficult crime to prove in the court of law. It is a horrible crime that affects not just the victim but their family too, and in many cases it affects the family of the accused. And a false accusation is just as bad. Sadly, both the victim and the falsely accused are branded for life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6234538633154045478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220350174?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385676298" href="/book/show/11060268-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-electronic">own-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220350174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5701835114900256905">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I tried to explain the plot of this book to several of my friends at school, and while some times it went successfully, there were other times when it didn't. On the surface, <i>You Against Me</i> is about Mikey, whose fifteen-year-old sister, Karyn, has been raped. The young man charged with raping her, Tom, also also has a younger sister named Ellie. Mikey and Ellie meet each other and begin to form a bond, but their connection may bring devastating consequences.<br/><br/>When examining this book bey</span>
  <span id="freeText5701835114900256905" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />I tried to explain the plot of this book to several of my friends at school, and while some times it went successfully, there were other times when it didn't. On the surface, <i>You Against Me</i> is about Mikey, whose fifteen-year-old sister, Karyn, has been raped. The young man charged with raping her, Tom, also also has a younger sister named Ellie. Mikey and Ellie meet each other and begin to form a bond, but their connection may bring devastating consequences.<br /><br />When examining this book beyond its surface, its about many different things: family, loyalty, love, doing the right thing, etc. It doesn't focus on the victim of the rape or the rapist himself, rather, it shows the perforating effect of the act on those standing in the periphery. Packed with pathos, this book will make you feel the emotion and the tension as the conflict climbs higher and higher.<br /><br />However, <i>You Against Me</i> had its faults. The story seemed like it was floundering and going nowhere in some sections, but in others I was wishing Downham had described the drama in more detail. The romance, while good, was questionable - both of your siblings are involved in a rape and you decide to go make out? It felt a tad rushed and unrealistic. Finally, none of the characters were likable. Not sure if that could be considered a bad thing, but at times I wanted to reach into my Kindle and let loose some serious slapping.<br /><br />Overall, a unique book in terms of how the scenario of rape is handled, as it shows the process of the families coping as opposed to the victim and the accused themselves. I wouldn't recommend it to any random person I met on the street, but if the plot summary grabs your attention, I would recommend you give it a try.<br /><br />*cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>

<div id="review_115810028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115810028" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393730599p2/1894085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115810028?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=to-reread">to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=uk">uk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115810028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer924906740998043842">I had high expectations before I started this book. I can safely say my expectations were pretty much met. The book didn't blow my mind or leave me emotional. (Not to say the book didn't make me feel anything. There were times I was happy and angry and <i>worried</i>.) But for the most part, I had a calm feeling. The setting even felt calming. I liked that.<br/><br/>I thought the author did great with the characters and relationships. They felt realistic and believable. There were times when some of the characte</span>
  <span id="freeText924906740998043842" style="display:none">I had high expectations before I started this book. I can safely say my expectations were pretty much met. The book didn't blow my mind or leave me emotional. (Not to say the book didn't make me feel anything. There were times I was happy and angry and <i>worried</i>.) But for the most part, I had a calm feeling. The setting even felt calming. I liked that.<br /><br />I thought the author did great with the characters and relationships. They felt realistic and believable. There were times when some of the characters would say or do something that pissed me off. I thought they were being unfair, selfish, or stupid. But then later on, those same characters would say something that made me completely understand why they said what they said or why they did what they did. I'm glad for that. I never like going through books hating characters.<br /><br />As for the main characters, Mikey and Ellie, I really liked them. I thought their relationship was done well. My favorite line in the book was from Ellie's brother Tom, the one being accused of the crime. He said this: "You want this to be a love story?" Well, I know I wanted it to be, between Mikey and Ellie. And after reading it, I think it is and more. The book's summary states it perfectly: <i>'It's a book about loyalty and the choices that come with it. But above all it's a book about love - for one's family and for another.'</i><br /><br />Not everything is resolved by the end of the book. We don't exactly know what will happen to the characters, but it's not that hard to imagine. I don't believe the author left us hanging, which I'm grateful for. And like I mentioned before, the ending even left me with a calm feeling. So for me, it was a satisfying read, and I definitely recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="924906740998043842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_457617592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457617592" />
    <a title="♥ Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah"><img alt="♥ Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455167556p2/13161862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457617592?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Sarah" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah">♥ Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13161862-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457617592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8770138311535234074"><b>Warning: Possible spoilers, but not really. Also, kind of a long rant and full of complaints – continue if you're contemplating on reading this. Otherwise, you might want to skip this review.</b><br/><br/>***<br/><br/>Initially, I was intrigued and instantly drawn to the premise, because rape was being explored through the eyes of the victim's brother and the perpetrator's sister. Further, issues of loyalty, revenge, forbidden- <i>Romeo & Juliet</i> type love, etc. were brought up. However, these themes were never fully flesh</span>
  <span id="freeText8770138311535234074" style="display:none"><b>Warning: Possible spoilers, but not really. Also, kind of a long rant and full of complaints – continue if you're contemplating on reading this. Otherwise, you might want to skip this review.</b><br /><br />***<br /><br />Initially, I was intrigued and instantly drawn to the premise, because rape was being explored through the eyes of the victim's brother and the perpetrator's sister. Further, issues of loyalty, revenge, forbidden- <i>Romeo &amp; Juliet</i> type love, etc. were brought up. However, these themes were never fully fleshed out; but were rather, watered down by the cheesy and unbelievable "forbidden romance" with the enemy. <br /><br />My initial enthusiasm quickly died down and turned bitter, as both Mikey and Ellie turned out to be completely unlikable characters. Objectively, I could see the <i>intention</i> behind the romance aspect, as well as the choices Ellie made toward the end, but it was executed poorly; and I wasn't convinced she handled it appropriately. <br /> <br />Additionally, Ellie &amp; Mikey's relationship felt unbearable. I was cringing through the contrite, forced, cheesy dialogue. And Mikey's declaration of his "feelings" toward his supposed enemy? Unforgivable. Unrealistic. Unbelievable. <br /><br />Also, I expected some angst: raw anger and the true heart of revenge from Mikey, yet he turned out to be weak and selfish, just like Ellie. I didn't really feel any brotherly/sister love from either of them either. They were just flat characters. <br /><br />But it was interesting that Karyn wasn't depicted as the innocent, shy, bright, studious type that simply got taken advantage of. However, what <u>pissed me off</u> was how she was described: drinking, partying, boy-crazy (but who isn't at 15?), wearing that <i>short skirt</i>. . . WHOA. Was that supposed to make me question the validity of Karyn's statement/allegation? Because those "reasons" hardly justifies rape. <br /><br />And although Karyn wasn't necessarily likable in the story, I would have rather read about her than her sorry ass brother and his childish endeavors. <br /><br />Also, I never once believed Tom was innocent, so I couldn't help but despise Ellie more after her little confession. Without the confession, I could have sympathized with her and her means of "coping" by trashing Karyn, but that wasn't the case. Ellie knew the truth. Also, the <i>way in which</i> Ellie handled the truth also upset me, and I couldn't help but feel she was motivated by some petty romance with the enemy; and if guilt, sense of responsibility or truth were behind her actions – I didn't notice. <br /><br />Lastly, I struggled with the British terminology/slang/lingo. Like, what the hell does a <i>fag</i> mean? I'm guessing either a cigarette or a blunt? There were just, a lot of other little references and words I didn't quite get, which added to my frustrations with this book. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>Overall:</b><br /><br />1. I didn't once believe Karyn was lying. <br /><br />2. I really disliked all the characters, except Jacko. He was OK, but he was in less than 1 percent of the story. <br /><br />3. The romance was contrived, silly and most of all, <i>unbelievable </i>. I just didn't buy any of it. If my brother told me he was "in love" with the sister of the guy that raped me after only meeting her a total of 10 times, I would FREAK. It was just too absurd. Also, it would have been a lot of more interesting to read if Mikey's intent was to seek <i>revenge</i> on Tom by messing with his "innocent" sister (Ellie), rather than to just seek "info" from her. That was lame! <br /><br />4. It might have been more interesting if Tom &amp; Ellie were close friends with Mikey &amp; Karyn <i><u>before</u> the alleged rape</i>. If Mikey and Ellie already had a romantic relationship before the incident, then I would have been more understanding/ sympathetic to their relationship. Also, it would have been a hell of a lot more dramatic. <br /><br />5. I guess the "results" of trial wasn't mentioned because the story was mainly about Mikey and Ellie. Still, I would've liked to know. That was important to me. At least give me that. I need some sort of justice... I didn't get any kind of closure at all. Disappointing. <br /><br />6. I appreciated the "public" response and how the kids at school started taking sides and so forth. It was all ugly and unfair and unfortunate. As messy and ugly it all was though, it seemed realistic and accurate. However, there still wasn't enough meat in the story overall to keep me interested. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>I was extremely disappointed; <i>You against me</i> was a total miss for me. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8770138311535234074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145255434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145255434" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145255434?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385751605" href="/book/show/9972776-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers who enjoyed Stolen by Lucy Christopher and Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=glad-i-gave-it-a-chance">glad-i-gave-it-a-chance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=couldn-t-stop-reading-it">couldn-t-stop-reading-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=writing-to-which-i-aspire">writing-to-which-i-aspire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=covers-i-love">covers-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=surprisingly-liked">surprisingly-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=stories-with-a-message">stories-with-a-message</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=stories-that-challenge-me">stories-that-challenge-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145255434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18008089857526025911"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me' title='You Against Me by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>You Against Me</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/628636.Jenny_Downham' title='Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Downham</a> (author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die' title='Before I Die by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Die</a>) is one of those books where the book blurb reminds you a lot of a <i>Lifetime</i> movie. You have a boy and a girl, joined by the sordid details of a crime and accusation involving their siblings. The boy is planning revenge in some form while the girl, unaware of the boy's intentions or identity, slowly begins to fall for him. It almost sounds like <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> meets a <i>Dateline</i> crime special. How can this end well on either side?<br/><br/>Mikey is str</span>
  <span id="freeText18008089857526025911" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me" title="You Against Me by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">You Against Me</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/628636.Jenny_Downham" title="Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Downham</a> (author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die" title="Before I Die by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Die</a>) is one of those books where the book blurb reminds you a lot of a <i>Lifetime</i> movie. You have a boy and a girl, joined by the sordid details of a crime and accusation involving their siblings. The boy is planning revenge in some form while the girl, unaware of the boy's intentions or identity, slowly begins to fall for him. It almost sounds like <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> meets a <i>Dateline</i> crime special. How can this end well on either side?<br /><br />Mikey is struggling to balance work and family as he copes with the aftermath of his sister Karyn's alleged rape. Though his dreams lie in living in London and learning to become a chef, he instead toils away to help his family because his single mother is an alcoholic who spends more time hung-over than with her three children. What were the fraying threads of his family life now threaten to rip apart entirely after what happens to Karyn; police officers and social workers become parts of the family's life, much to Mikey"s dismay. But even though the future is unclear, Mikey knows one thing: <i>Thomas Parker caused all of this.</i><br /><br />Thomas "Tom" Parker is Ellie Parker's older brother -- the one who was accused of raping Karyn. Though her family hides behind the gates leading to their home, Ellie too is dealing with a family on the brink of self-destructing. Because the allegations against Tom are of the "he said, she said" variety, Ellie feels a great pressure since she was home the night the alleged rape occurred, and she will likely be detrimental to her brother's defense in the upcoming trial. However much her parents assure her that helping her brother prove his innocence is the right thing, Ellie feels even more doubtful and uncertain the longer she processes the memories of that night and the truth of what really happened. . .<br /><br />Mikey and Ellie meet under the guise of lies and a pursuit for revenge. Their initial relationship is based more of Mikey's attempt to glean his own personal justice upon Tom, but nothing works quite as planned once Mikey and Ellie begin to realize that <i>they like each other.</i> Whatever their differences or flaws, they are connected by the crime and its ripple effects through both of their families. How will they survive it? And will they be able to look at each other the same way after the fact?<br /><br /><i>You Against Me</i> is definitely a very fascinating book, especially with how it delves into the psychology of how families cope with crimes (from aspects of both accuser and accused). . .but it is also very frustrating. No, this book is not a romance -- or, at least, not in the traditional sense. Instead, it's a portrait of realism, falsehood, truth, fear, doubt, family, and healing. The characters don't take easy paths -- and, even when decisions are made, the answers are not so clear-cut and simple. This is an ambiguous book showcasing that there are always two sides to every story and that, instead of black and white, our world is a very gray place of villains masquerading as heroes and heroes being portrayed as villains.<br /><br />However much I loved this book for challenging my mind and my own judgments, I honestly don't think it's a book for everyone. It's the type of story that you mull over, that you ponder and contemplate, that makes you think, <i>"Okay, what would I do?"</i> Not every reader is comfortable with that kind of introspection, so that's why I hesitate to say,"YOU MUST READ IT." Still, <i>You Against Me</i> is very fascinating and thought-provoking, so I hope it will find the readers who will appreciate it the most -- and who come away better and stronger because of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18008089857526025911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_204088912" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204088912" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204088912?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204088912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1503095054470169069">This issue alone would usually have me steer clear of a book like this. I'm a paranormal junkie and the occasional contempory romance YA reader, but when it comes to serious issues I tend to stay away...I guess I like reading escape more then reality, but once in awhile a book comes along and you read the reviews and my curiosity seems to get the better of me. You Against Me is one of those books and I'm so glad I took the chance on this one since I would have missed out on a really great read.<br/><br/><b>Y</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1503095054470169069" style="display:none">This issue alone would usually have me steer clear of a book like this. I'm a paranormal junkie and the occasional contempory romance YA reader, but when it comes to serious issues I tend to stay away...I guess I like reading escape more then reality, but once in awhile a book comes along and you read the reviews and my curiosity seems to get the better of me. You Against Me is one of those books and I'm so glad I took the chance on this one since I would have missed out on a really great read.<br /><br /><b>You Against Me</b> is a story of pure complications. It's about a girl named Karyn who went to a party and is a victim of rape. Her brother Mikey, the has-to-be-responsible one in the family wants revenge on Tom, the one who did this to Karyn. But somewhere along the way Mikey falls for Tom's sister, Ellie. Someone who knows what actually happened... <br />That's a pretty messy situation huh? <br /><br />Jenny Downham did an amazing job of tackling this kind of issue. It's true that a lot of the time rape is a very hard to prove and there is a lot of he said/she said with dangling doubts in the background. But there is more to this story. We get to see what's it like for the other people involved, the families and how it effects their lives and the choices they make. It's about loyalty and right and wrong no matter how much you hate it. But it's also a story about finding love where you least expect it. <br />I didn't think a romance would be something that would fit in a story like this. It's so unlikely that the brother of the victim and the sister of the assaulter would come together like they did, but you know, it worked. I really enjoyed Mikey and Ellie. They are both going through their own personal hell, and yet, they don't want the other going through this pain, but by all rights, <i>should</i> want exactly that. They understand one another and no matter how problematic their relationship or involvement may seem, it makes more sense for them to be together then apart. It's not something easily conveyed but Downham did a very convincing job by combining an intricate issue with heartfelt hope. <br /><br />Overall, I was very impress with this book. We don't get all the answers in the end, but in a way I'm glad. I don't really know how I'd feel one way or the other regarding Tom but I think everything will be alright for the rest of the characters and that's good enough for me.<br /><br />Thought provoking, intriguing and tugs at the heart. <br />Highly recommended!<br /><br />(Are provided by Edelweiss) </span>
  <a data-text-id="1503095054470169069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
