<div id="review_162926026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162926026" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162926026?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385751605" href="/book/show/9972776-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=whoa-that-s-heavy">whoa-that-s-heavy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162926026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4784247507602839759"><b>Rating: 3.5</b><br/>I should have written a review for this one awhile back but to be honest I didn't know what to say exactly. It is no doubt a powerful novel and I wanted to make sure I would say the right things... well time has gone by and I still don't know what to say so here goes nothing.<br/><br/>Now for those of you who don't know the premise it's a <i>twisted</i> one. Mikey has a sister named Karyn and Ellie has a brother named Tom. Karyn has accused Tom of raping her. Well Mikey can't stand for that, so to get</span>
  <span id="freeText4784247507602839759" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 3.5</b><br />I should have written a review for this one awhile back but to be honest I didn't know what to say exactly. It is no doubt a powerful novel and I wanted to make sure I would say the right things... well time has gone by and I still don't know what to say so here goes nothing.<br /><br />Now for those of you who don't know the premise it's a <i>twisted</i> one. Mikey has a sister named Karyn and Ellie has a brother named Tom. Karyn has accused Tom of raping her. Well Mikey can't stand for that, so to get to Tom Mikey tries to befriend Ellie. Can we see where this is going? Yes, Mikey falls for Ellie and vice versa. Ouch, see isn't that just a sticky situation? Sorry, I probably confused you, but I promise in the book it's not that hard to follow.<br /><br />The backdrop of this story is in England and I have to say I was having trouble keeping up with some of the dialogue. It's easy enough it's just I am so picky about knowing the <i>exact</i> meaning of everything so this Yank was just a tad bit frustrated with herself. It does add to the certain atmosphere though, and was cool to see. Now on to the characters, and oh boy the characters. They are the main reason why I kept flip flopping on my star rating. I would have to say I hated each and every one of them at some point in the book, which I would have to assume to be accurate for a situation like this. They are all, to put it bluntly, screwed up. Ellie struggles to be loyal to her brother. She keeps remembering the good in him, but there is also the bad side too. The author did a superb job of showing how Ellie waged this internal war and I am willing to admit I wouldn't want to be in her place. Mikey on the other hand deals with the situation badly. He wants to help Karyn but in all the wrong ways. Out of the two characters he was my favorite. He tries so hard to do right, but can't seem to get it and I can applaud someone like that.<br /><br />Mikey and Ellie take turns showing their perspectives, but it's done in third person so the format was definitely unique. Both the main characters may live in the same country but it might as well feel like different worlds. Mikey lives in a rundown apartment with a mom who is a drunk, and he feels the responsibility of caring for his two younger sisters. He isn't perfect in the least though, he notices how much Karyn actually helped him shoulder the burden. Then there is Ellie who comes from a privileged family. For goodness sakes her parents gave her brother a welcoming party for being released from jail! So you see, two worlds apart but the two worlds collide when Mikey and Ellie are together.<br /><br />I know this is going to sound heartless of me, but the biggest downfall of the novel I would say is the romance. Now please before you say your boos hear me out. I'm trying to be realistic here, and I believe for a <b>healthy</b> relationship to evolve you need more time and trust. And I can't see this being an ideal situation for that. It could happen but I doubt in the pace that it did. Others will love the romance but it didn't do it for me. <br /><br />The subject of rape is never an easy topic to dig into, but I feel the author did it justice. She made the story expand by making the main characters people who are close to the victim but not the victim themselves. It shows how far reaching the effects are. The author isn't skimpy on details and I must admit it was excruciating to read. There is so much meat in this story and I could go on even more, but suffice to say that the story is layered and feels complex, and most importantly is able to expose some important truths.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4784247507602839759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135800467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135800467" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135800467?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=mixed">mixed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135800467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9739520022638920390">I wanted to read this book from the moment I heard about it.. But, while waiting for it to be published, I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die' title='Before I Die by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Die</a> first (and I didn't really liked it) so I didn't know if to read "You Against Me" after all, no matter how many good reviews I've seen. <br/><br/>But.. yesterday I gave it a try and now I can't stop wondering <i>why in the world didn't I read it earlier?</i><br/>It was <i>that</i> good.<br/><br/>The <b>title</b> is perfect - and it doesn't define only the relation between Ellie and Mickey, but also the relation betwee</span>
  <span id="freeText9739520022638920390" style="display:none">I wanted to read this book from the moment I heard about it.. But, while waiting for it to be published, I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die" title="Before I Die by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Die</a> first (and I didn't really liked it) so I didn't know if to read "You Against Me" after all, no matter how many good reviews I've seen. <br><br>But.. yesterday I gave it a try and now I can't stop wondering <i>why in the world didn't I read it earlier?</i><br>It was <i>that</i> good.<br><br>The <b>title</b> is perfect - and it doesn't define only the relation between Ellie and Mickey, but also the relation between all the characters because at some point there is always someone against the other one -they always make choices and they are left to deal with the consequences.<br>I loved the fact that this was not a fairytale and every action they made was getting them to some place new, every time they tried to fix something, there was another thing that went wrong.. I felt like watching a movie, I found myself reading in a 'fast-forward mode' (or so it felt) because there were so many things happening. There were even so moments when I found myself asking <i> Aah, tell me again how did they get to this point? </i> and I kept reading with my mouth wide open.<br><br>Before reading it, I thought that the story would be about who was saying the truth and who was lying - and maybe in a way this is true. <br>But I was surprised to see that this story was more about <b>choices, and family, and loyalty, and love, and trust</b>.. about finding the soft line between what's right and what's wrong - because what was right for someone it was always wrong for the other. <br><br><b>Mickey</b> is trying to take care of his family ( his sister Karyn going through such a rough time, his little sister so innocent of all this, his mother that couldn't cope with all that happened and lost herself into drinking). Even though he is older than Karyn he makes a childish decision - to kick Tom's ass, as if this would make up for what his sister was going through. <br>But meeting Tom's little sister and starting to care for her it's something that he never thought would happen, and so they get thrown into such a difficult situation - they are so different and have such a different purpose: she is rich, he is not.. but more than that she is a witness in the trial, and what she says can change everything.<br><br><b>Ellie</b> in a way is trying to just the same thing - take care of her brother - but more than that she wants to get through the trial and be free again. <br>Her family has as many problems as Mickey's, even though money are not on that list.<br>The father is as cold as ice, her mother has no voice up until the end, and Ellie's brother is in big, big trouble and his life depends on what his little sister knows.<br>But does anyone think about what Ellie wants? Does anyone care about her needs? She is just a child and she feels completely alone until she meets Mickey.<br><br>Now I must say that there some things that I really liked about this book:<br><br>#1 - the love story - there was such a smooth transition between the moment they met, the moment they realized how much they liked each other and the moment they knew they were in love. It was some kind of modern "Romeo &amp; Juliet" story, and I wanted so badly for them to figure out a way to be together, to make things right again and just enjoy being together.<br><br>#2 - the fact that being from "different teams" in this trial and being involved with each other didn't get unnoticed. And the consequences were somehow realistic. <br><br>#3 - the relation between the members of each family. I loved to see how Mickey's family found a way to change some things, and it was hard not to understand the situation in Ellie's family even at the end. I keep thinking about them all and I should congratulate the author for handling so well this situation because it was damn difficult. I know, I make no sense but it's hard to keep this review spoiler free.<br><br>#4 - the characters - they were all described very well. I wouldn't want to be in their shoes, but I could understand them (or most of them). It was great to see how one's decision could change other's life, and they changed through the story, and they picked sides, and they did things and had to deal with consequences... and at the end they all understood. (and I won't say more)<br><br>Even if there is not a clear ending, it was perfect for the story. <br>I wanted to know what happened next (I still want), I wanted some more answers, but it also gave me hope.. and this is enough.<br><br>All in one, this is a great book - amazing - and full of emotions ... it's one of those books that make you think <i>what would you do?</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jenny-downham/you-against-me-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

<div id="review_211407726" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211407726" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211407726?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385751605" href="/book/show/9972776-you-against-me">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211407726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12346272360391071647">This story is about two families affected by the accusation of rape. It doesn't focus on the accused and accuser, but rather on the sister and brother of the two parties. <br/><br/>This story is told from two perspectives: Mikey McKenzie, the older brother of the accuser, Karyn, and Ellie Parker the younger sister of the accused, Tom. The story opens up with Mikey trying to figure out how to make Tom pay for what he's done to his sister. Mikey feels he needs to do something because since the rape, Karyn r</span>
  <span id="freeText12346272360391071647" style="display:none">This story is about two families affected by the accusation of rape. It doesn't focus on the accused and accuser, but rather on the sister and brother of the two parties. <br /><br />This story is told from two perspectives: Mikey McKenzie, the older brother of the accuser, Karyn, and Ellie Parker the younger sister of the accused, Tom. The story opens up with Mikey trying to figure out how to make Tom pay for what he's done to his sister. Mikey feels he needs to do something because since the rape, Karyn refuses to set foot out of their flat or go to school. She barely changes clothes or eats. Tom has just been released on bail, and Mikey figures this would be an ideal opportunity to make a move. Tom has no idea what Mikey looks like so he heads over to the Parker's home to scout it out. When he knocks on the door, Ellie answers, she's the same age as Karyn and doesn't recognize Mikey, mistakes him for one of Tom's college friends and invites him to Tom's release party. Mikey does go to the party but he never gets a chance alone with Tom. He instead ends up talking to Ellie most of the night and from that he hatches a plan to cozy up to her and pump her for information. She was, after all in the house when the attack occurred, and he doesn't believe for one minute, the statement she gave the police: that she saw nothing. This plan sort of backfires when Tom starts to fall for Ellie and Ellie starts to fall for him. Will their relationship survive when the truth comes out?<br /><br />I loved Mikey and Ellie' story. There were some <i>swoon-worthy</i> scenes. It's ironic that out of all the people in the world they end up falling for each other. I think because of the shared experience, even though on opposite sides, they have a bond. They both can understand what the other is going through. All the way around, this would be a difficult situation. You don't even know who's telling the truth until about two thirds through the book, but even then there is damage to both families no matter what. Rape, as a crime is such a difficult one to prosecute and without definitive proof there would always be a shadow of doubt cast on both sides. Even with this tough subject, I highly recommend this story. I thoroughly enjoyed it! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12346272360391071647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187294867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187294867" />
    <a title="Steffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3472833-steffy"><img alt="Steffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440260341p2/3472833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187294867?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steffy" href="/user/show/3472833-steffy">Steffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187294867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1296756192520687107">Honestly I’m not sure how I feel about that book. I can’t say I despised it it would be pushing it and I can’t say I liked it…it would be too nice. When I finished my initial reaction was “Ehhhhh” which for the people who know me means ‘not terrible but could have been so much better’ in Steph’s language. <br/>No Seriously, I don’t know if I went there with too high of an expectation, I read the summary a few months ago and was just dying to read it since then. I expected something like Leaving Parad</span>
  <span id="freeText1296756192520687107" style="display:none">Honestly I’m not sure how I feel about that book. I can’t say I despised it it would be pushing it and I can’t say I liked it…it would be too nice. When I finished my initial reaction was “Ehhhhh” which for the people who know me means ‘not terrible but could have been so much better’ in Steph’s language. <br />No Seriously, I don’t know if I went there with too high of an expectation, I read the summary a few months ago and was just dying to read it since then. I expected something like Leaving Paradise by Simone Elkeles (If you didn’t read it yet, just do…you’re still here? You are not listening (sigh). Very well lets continue) but it was not. First of all the language is very crude, not that I mind but it’s definitely not for younger teens…I wouldn’t advise it to anyone under the age of 15.<br />The setting was great the storyline was…okay even if there were some inconsistencies in it. What bothered me the most was the characters. Usually when I read a book I really get into it, the emotions are there but here it didn’t do it for me. I couldn’t feel bad for Karyn the ‘victim’ who really was only good at whining, I couldn’t hate the ‘criminal’ or anything. There was no real back story. Why is Mickey’s mom an alcoholic? Why is Tom snapping like that alkl the time? Why is Ellie’s father so hard on her and not on Tom? How does it make her feel? I didn’t like any of the characters much and just went along with the story for the sake of it. I found the characters plain and the absence of characterization made it boring. Ellie and Mickey relationship is also…so generic. Why did she like him? Why did she just go along with it? It’s just so…<br />I won’t lie; the book also has its moments. There are a couple of emotional scenes but I’m not sure it’s worth buying. But once again I might have set my expectation so high that I could only feel being let down. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1296756192520687107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_142227732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142227732" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142227732?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125405842" />
    <a title="Dija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2857113-dija"><img alt="Dija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360335537p2/2857113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125405842?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125405842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8712171891342086656">Reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me' title='You Against Me by Jenny Downham' rel='nofollow noopener'>You Against Me</a> was like listening to a recording on high speed. All the characters' reactions seemed extreme and drastic and I couldn't understand where they were coming from at all. Downham seemed to be trying way too hard to make her characters seem relatable but they ended up seeming stiff and orchestrated instead. <br/><br/>Maybe my life's too sheltered, but I simply couldn't see this story happening in RL. It wasn't brutal enough to be believable and it wasn't normal enough to be realistic ei</span>
  <span id="freeText8712171891342086656" style="display:none">Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8720917.You_Against_Me" title="You Against Me by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">You Against Me</a> was like listening to a recording on high speed. All the characters' reactions seemed extreme and drastic and I couldn't understand where they were coming from at all. Downham seemed to be trying way too hard to make her characters seem relatable but they ended up seeming stiff and orchestrated instead. <br /><br />Maybe my life's too sheltered, but I simply couldn't see this story happening in RL. It wasn't brutal enough to be believable and it wasn't normal enough to be realistic either. I could tell that Downham's intentions were to write a deep and touching story, but I was mostly bored throughout.<br /><br />Nearly all of the characters' problems were blown way out of proportion and had one simple solution - communication. Everyone in this novel lived in his or her own little bubble, away from reality, and didn't really bother explaining their feelings, choosing to have a pity party and lashing out bizarrely instead. <br /><br />Overall, this was a meaningless book and I doubt I'll be reading Downham's other works. Put simply, her writing style doesn't appeal to me and I have trouble relating to her characters.<br /><br />1.5/5 stars<br /><br /><b>For more reviews, visit my <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.</b></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_155198753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155198753" />
    <a title="Katya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4324634-katya"><img alt="Katya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155198753?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katya" href="/user/show/4324634-katya">Katya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155198753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10969831111718016760">This review is harder to write than I thought.<br/><br/>Seriously, I've started and erased it enough times to have written it twice. Alas, I am short on words, have been for quite some time, so forgive me if this doesn't come off as particularly articulate or... well... making sense.<br/><br/>I discovered "Speak" last September, following the 'soft porn' debacle, and fell in love with Laurie Halse Anderson's writing. Her books are always centered around difficult, touchy topics, but you can't say for a single minut</span>
  <span id="freeText10969831111718016760" style="display:none">This review is harder to write than I thought.<br /><br />Seriously, I've started and erased it enough times to have written it twice. Alas, I am short on words, have been for quite some time, so forgive me if this doesn't come off as particularly articulate or... well... making sense.<br /><br />I discovered "Speak" last September, following the 'soft porn' debacle, and fell in love with Laurie Halse Anderson's writing. Her books are always centered around difficult, touchy topics, but you can't say for a single minute that it's just for shock factor. The subjects of rape, anorexia, guilt, depression are handled with sensitivity and respect not seen very often. Anderson is one of those few authors who write for teenagers without talking down on their audience, a phenomenon which has become, sadly, very prominent in YA.<br /><br />I'm telling you all this because I like Anderson very much, and that has made me compare books with an even slightly similar premise to hers. That might be the reason why I had such a hard time liking "You Against Me".<br /><br />Now, don't get me wrong - I'm not saying that Jenny Downham doesn't handle her subject matter with the utmost respect. Quite on the contrary. She leads us into a world of subjective truth, one where it's one person's word against the other. She doesn't just show us how the victim of the alleged rape, Karyn, feels, but also the impact the event has on her family, and also on the rapist, Tom, and his family. Karyn's reality is a fragile one, because she falls victim to many of the questions raised when it comes to date rape: "Did she really not consent?", "Did she not invite sex in the way she dresses?", "Should she have gotten drunk?".<br /><br />Incidentally, I read this a little before I heard of Kenneth Clarke's remarks on the different "degrees" in rape. Perhaps I would have felt differently about this book if I'd waited a little.<br /><br />Here's the thing: Rape happens. One in every four women in the UK is assaulted each year, and in three forths of the cases, they suffer in the hands of someone they know - a relative, or a boyfriend, or even a friend. No matter who the rapist is, there is always the violation of the body, the violation of the mind, and in the case of date rape, the violation of trust. No, it doesn't matter how she was dressed. No, it doesn't matter if she flirted. And especially if she was drunk. In fact, having sex with a woman when she's clearly inebrated and unable to take care of herself is horrible because she trusted herself in your care. Those are the themes in "You Against Me", and they are supported perfectly.<br /><br />Also, I enjoyed how Downham developed the character of Ellie, how she showed her struggle between loyalty for her family and desire to tell the truth. It's another side of the problem, guilt, and it's not often portrayed in books.<br /><br />So why didn't I like it? <br /><br />Honestly, I wished the writing would grab me more. The pacing of the book is fine around the end, but they could have cut out fifty pages around the middle and wouldn't have lost anything. <br /><br />The other thing is that while Ellie's character is superb, the others fall pretty flat and two-dimensional. There's not enough complexity to them, and that makes up for some difficult reading. I would have liked to see more of Tom, or his father, more of Mikey's mother, hell, more of Karyn. If this was more of a character study book, like "Gone, Gone, Gone", it would have made up for some sluggishness in the plot.<br /><br />All in all, it's a good book, with some very important messages and themes. It is written well, and if you're a fan of a slow-burn kind of plot, I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10969831111718016760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271211928?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271211928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1566220570602112055"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>WARNING: MESSY REVIEW AND A BIT SPOILERY!<br/><br/>Actually, I really don't know what to say. *sigh* This was a compelling and powerful read but after I finished the book, for some unknown reason I don't know what to feel. Actually, I still haven't figured out my overall and final say about this book but I'll give you my initial thoughts while I was reading it.<br/><br/>You Against Me was a novel that discussed a delicate and tricky issue. I may have steered clear of this book after seeing the blurb since </span>
  <span id="freeText1566220570602112055" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />WARNING: MESSY REVIEW AND A BIT SPOILERY!<br /><br />Actually, I really don't know what to say. *sigh* This was a compelling and powerful read but after I finished the book, for some unknown reason I don't know what to feel. Actually, I still haven't figured out my overall and final say about this book but I'll give you my initial thoughts while I was reading it.<br /><br />You Against Me was a novel that discussed a delicate and tricky issue. I may have steered clear of this book after seeing the blurb since it sounds a little dramatic and complicated. But as I read it, it wasn't really at all like that and I did like the plot and characters. The book tells the story of Mikey, brother of the accuser of being raped and Ellie sister of the accused. And as you may have guessed, yes, they fell in love with each other. <br /><br />The story was told in multiple POVs, both of Ellie and Mikey but in a third person. I liked both characters but between the two I find it easier to read and connect with Mickey. I understand that he was always really trying to help his sister and her family but made it in a lot of wrong ways. And I was glad that by the end of the book he completely realized it. I loved it that between him and Ellie he was the one thinking more positive that their relationship has a chance and that he was the one fighting more. Ellie, on the other hand seems to be a little unpredictable. Though it was pretty understandable since she's torn between the choices of protecting her brother or telling the truth. In the end though, she was able to pick the right choice and stick to it. The romance between the two was moving and I adored it though I wished it have been discussed more deeper.<br /><br />I really admire Jenny Downham for being able to discuss the issues of rape well, especially how she confer the effects of it for the families of both sides. As I was reading this I find myself a little torn between the two families. I saw the struggles of each family to protect their loved ones. I actually felt pity over Ellie's family since I saw how desperate they were trying to keep their family together and for some reasons I admired Ellie's relationship with his brother. I know Tom's guilty but I saw that he was having regrets over it and despite Ellie's choice of telling the truth he cared for her more. I was actually really touched by it.<br /><br />I had a lot of understanding about the issue after reading this. However there were really a lot of loose ends, I even thought maybe there is a sequel. Maybe that's why I still can't think of my final thought of this book.<br /><br />Alright, this is really a messy review! Maybe I'll update this soon once I finally gathered my final thoughts. <br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://bookoverdose.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1566220570602112055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

When Mikey and Ellie meet, two worlds collide</i><br/><br/>Sounds interesting enough right? WRONG!<br/>The blurb is far more interesting than the book itself. The ink was blue"</i><br/>It was useless sentences like this that made the book so boring. <br/><br/>Mikey'</span>
  <span id="freeText11810577325966764956" style="display:none"><b>Plot:</b> <i>Mikey's sister says a boy raped her. Ellie's brother says he didn't do it. When Mikey and Ellie meet, two worlds collide</i><br /><br />Sounds interesting enough right? WRONG!<br />The blurb is far more interesting than the book itself. The book concentrated on all the useless things we didn't want to know about. The plot was very weak, it was just plain boring. <br /><i>"She wrote her name on the top of the sheet and underlined it. The ink was blue"</i><br />It was useless sentences like this that made the book so boring. <br /><br />Mikey's sister claims she got raped. Naturally any brother would be angry. Mikey's only 18, I totally understand but when you're mother isn't capable of standing on her own two feet let alone look after the family you're forced to step up, which means you don't waste your time thinking up ridiculous plots to avenge your sister who in the end didn't appreciate it anyway and called you stupid and selfish. (Talk about ungrateful)<br /><br />Ellie. Oh god where to begin? I hated her from the moment she was first introduced. If your brother is accused of rape, shouldn't you be less ignorant and more cautious about life? According to Ellie no. After a stupid fight in school she unbuttons her school shirt , lifts her skirt higher and texts a boy she barely -no correction- <b>doesn't</b> know to meet her in a cemetery! Oh and better yet, later on she strips in front of him and goes swimming in a lake. Let's not forget after she finds out who this mystery boy is she invites him to her house -knowing nobody would be home- gives him dope, makes him drink wine, takes him to her bedroom and takes her top off, all in the hopes of getting information from him! Is she mad?! She didn't know the kind of guy Mikey was! Not only did she invite him to her house when she knew nobody would be home she gave him alcohol and dope! I mean for godsakes, this kind of stupidity leaves you questioning her mental stability! <br /><br />Writing was boring, useless and unnecessary parts in the majority of the book and just plain bad! </span>

<div id="review_127522413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127522413" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063483-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297346517p2/4063483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127522413?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063483-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063483-beth?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063483-beth?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063483-beth?shelf=january-2011">january-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127522413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10591386258689669609">If I'm honest, this book is probably more of a 3.5/5 for me, but it definitely doesn't deserve to be dropped to a 3.<br/><br/>Downham's writing is superb. I hated Before I Die, but You Against Me is a lot more basic, stripped down, interesting and realistic. There's no florid language to draw an artificial reaction out of you; this is two characters and a situation. This is gritty, heartfelt and honest. The characters are lovingly drawn and flawed, but relatable. The ending is a great balance between hope</span>
  <span id="freeText10591386258689669609" style="display:none">If I'm honest, this book is probably more of a 3.5/5 for me, but it definitely doesn't deserve to be dropped to a 3.<br /><br />Downham's writing is superb. I hated Before I Die, but You Against Me is a lot more basic, stripped down, interesting and realistic. There's no florid language to draw an artificial reaction out of you; this is two characters and a situation. This is gritty, heartfelt and honest. The characters are lovingly drawn and flawed, but relatable. The ending is a great balance between hopeful and not so picture perfect. I was initially disappointed that we didn't get to see the trial, but ultimately it was the right decision. Also, I was one of the people who believed that Downham couldn't pull the premise off without it seeming forced and contrived. It didn't. It was plausible and believable.<br /><br />But there was one huge problem with the book that I just couldn't get past. It's something that seems much more rife in English novels that any other: the concept that the middle classes are evil. Very much Screw The Rules, I Have Money. While the lower classes are hardworking and truthful - flawed, yes, but still One Of Us. <br /><br />This problem was present in its highest order in YAM. I never once believed that Tom was innocent. This is coming from someone who is ridiculously objective about rape. I am "innocent until proven guilty" the whole way. But Ellie's father was one hair away from being a mustache-twirling villain. Karyn is a plot device, not a character; we see her maybe three times in total, and she's never asked to go through the details of her attack as Tom is. She's just there, and then she's proven right. Big deal. I didn't really care about her. That element of it was very one-sided and disappointing to me. But, still, a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10591386258689669609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144224616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144224616" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4615008-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579545470p2/4615008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144224616?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4615008-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma and other dark YA contemporary</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=gotten-rid-of">gotten-rid-of</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144224616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11394695142028147373"><a href='http://www.laurenreadsya.tumblr.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out my book blog for more reviews!</a><br/><br/>You Against Me is a intriguing, brilliantly written novel by the author of Before I Die. The cover makes it look like a love story, which it is not. Well, not just a love story. (The love story is good though. I need to stop saying ‘love story’ now. Okay.) It’s a story about relationships, not just between lovers, but between family members and friends too. It’s about loyalty, the truth, bravery, and how far we would go to protect the people we love. <br/><br/>I bou</span>
  <span id="freeText11394695142028147373" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.laurenreadsya.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out my book blog for more reviews!</a><br /><br />You Against Me is a intriguing, brilliantly written novel by the author of Before I Die. The cover makes it look like a love story, which it is not. Well, not just a love story. (The love story is good though. I need to stop saying ‘love story’ now. Okay.) It’s a story about relationships, not just between lovers, but between family members and friends too. It’s about loyalty, the truth, bravery, and how far we would go to protect the people we love. <br /><br />I bought this when it just came out in paperback, and I didn’t read it until now, because I didn’t remember Jenny Downham’s writing style very clearly from reading Before I Die so many years ago. I just wasn’t very excited about reading it, but I’m glad I eventually picked it up. I kept wanting to find out what really happened at that party, and which one—Karyn, the ‘victim’ or Tom, the ‘rapist’—was lying about it. And even though I thought I guessed which one was telling the truth, I was so wrong. <br /><br />The writing was flawless. There were no moments that I wished I could skim through because it was too detailed or complicated. She writes what she needed to write, and didn’t over-explain things. <br /><br />The title is perfect for this story. It isn’t only about the Mikey and Ellie’s relationships, but also that they’re on different teams. I thought the ending was good for this book. I don’t usually like open endings because I find it hard to imagine what happens after, but in this case, it was fitting. <br /><br />Blog post: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/17706984959/you-against-me-by-jenny-downham-review">http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/...</a></span>

<div id="review_133285283" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133285283" />
    <a title="Samantha Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4394330-samantha-young"><img alt="Samantha Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593532204p2/4394330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133285283?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha Young" href="/user/show/4394330-samantha-young">Samantha Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=covers-i-like">covers-i-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133285283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1431834089493339209">You Against Me is an incredible and beautiful addition to contemporary YA. Set in the UK, Jenny Downham gives a stunning portrayal of two families struggle to deal with the consequences of rape. Mikey and Ellie are our two main characters – Mikey is the brother of the rape victim and Ellie the sister of the accused. From the very beginning of the novel the reader does not know who is telling the truth and the more the facts unfold, the greater the emotional struggle becomes. What I loved most ab</span>
  <span id="freeText1431834089493339209" style="display:none">You Against Me is an incredible and beautiful addition to contemporary YA. Set in the UK, Jenny Downham gives a stunning portrayal of two families struggle to deal with the consequences of rape. Mikey and Ellie are our two main characters – Mikey is the brother of the rape victim and Ellie the sister of the accused. From the very beginning of the novel the reader does not know who is telling the truth and the more the facts unfold, the greater the emotional struggle becomes. What I loved most about Downham’s novel (second are the brilliantly drawn protagonists, so likeable and real) was the realistic and heartbreaking study of the consequences of the crime for the family of the accused. Most often in stories such as these the sympathy is of course with the victim and their family, but I found myself just as torn up for Ellie and her parents, as they fought with familial solidarity and doing what was right. Truly an amazing feat by a fantastic author. If you're a fan of Simone Elkeles, then this is a must read.<br /><br />Absolutely wonderful; made my chest ache with its painful brilliance.<br /><br />Five Massive Massive Stars!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1431834089493339209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x1rnOhIBcI6n1gQVLjH8PA7Sv83sm83kAXPDFm6H0c5MOt0+Xsl8PfhQAjwN4c0ZJ2P7nP1B+Ev9OFLRPjY4iQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17603345589298971179">Jenny Downham (born 1964) is a British novelist and an ex-actor. In her first book, Before I Die, the fictional account of the last few months of a sixteen-year-old girl who has been dying of leukemia for 4 years. The book is told in the first person. The book was acclaimed and was short-listed for the 2007 Guardian Award and the 2008 Lancashire Children's Book of the Year, nominated for the 2008 </span>
  <span id="freeText17603345589298971179" style="display:none">Jenny Downham (born 1964) is a British novelist and an ex-actor. In her first book, Before I Die, the fictional account of the last few months of a sixteen-year-old girl who has been dying of leukemia for 4 years. The book is told in the first person. The book was acclaimed and was short-listed for the 2007 Guardian Award and the 2008 Lancashire Children's Book of the Year, nominated for the 2008 Carnegie Medal and the 2008 Booktrust Teenage Prize, and won the 2008 Branford Boase Award.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17603345589298971179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
